Local News

City Chamber of Commerce and Various Trade Associations Jointly Telegraph Support for Legal Tender 60

Three Bank Notes Need to Increase Sharply Market Stabilizes Rice Prices City Government Strictly Prohibits Raising Prices

After the Ministry of Finance issued a public notice stating that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications were legal tender, and cash transactions were prohibited, the Issuing Reserve Committee held a meeting at 5:00 PM yesterday to draft operating rules, stipulating the standard exchange rate of the three banks for foreign currency, unlimited buying and selling of foreign currency, and the city government issued a public notice strictly prohibiting raising prices. The City Chamber of Commerce, various trade associations, and Yu Qiaqing, among others, sent telegrams of support. The Ministry of Finance completed its investigation of the cash reserves of various banks and money houses and ordered the exchange of legal tender for the three banks' banknotes according to the amounts. The need for the three banks' banknotes has increased sharply. Details are as follows:

Committee Prepares Rules

The Issuing Reserve Management Committee was established on the 4th, with Song Ziwen, Hu Bijiang, Chen Guangfu, Qian Xinzhi, and Li Jue elected as standing committee members, and Xu Kan and six others appointed to draft management and operating rules. Yesterday at 5:00 PM, Xu Kan convened the drafting committee members at the Central Bank's third-floor board meeting room for the drafting committee meeting. Xu Kan, Song Hanzhang, Zhang Gongquan, Tang Shoumin, Xu Xinliu, Li Fuzun, and Li Jue attended. Xu Kan chaired the meeting. The committee members expressed their opinions on the methods for exchanging silver dollars and silver for legal tender, as well as operating rules. The chairman summarized the opinions and drafted an outline, which will be submitted to the Issuing Reserve Management Committee for discussion and approval at the second meeting, before being submitted to the Imperial Ministry for approval and implementation. The meeting adjourned at 6:30 PM.

Ministry Completes Inspection of Bank and Money House Reserves

After the Ministry of Finance issued a public notice stating that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications were legal tender, it dispatched personnel yesterday morning to various banks in the city, including Zhejiang Xingye, Zhejiang Shiye, Kenye, Tongshang, China Industrial, Jincheng, Yanye, Dalu, Zhongnan, Siming, Shanghai, Guohua, Xinhua, Jiangsu, as well as the joint reserve of money houses, to investigate the total amount of cash reserves. This has been completed. The cash reserves, except for those sent to the Bank Preparation Management Committee to be used as reserves, may be exchanged for legal tender from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications according to the amounts.

Demand for Three Banks' Legal Tender Increases Sharply

After the new currency policy was implemented on the 4th, merchants and citizens complied with government decrees, using the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications as legal tender for all receipts and payments. Therefore, the demand for the three banks' banknotes increased sharply, especially for one-yuan notes. According to information from the Issuing Bureau of the Central Bank, on the 4th, the amount of one-yuan, five-yuan, and ten-yuan banknotes issued in this city alone reached approximately five million yuan. The issuance amounts of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications were both around one million yuan. As for the interior, although the Ministry has temporarily allowed the use of silver, the demand for banknotes has also increased. Branches of the three banks in various locations have sent telegrams requesting remittance, which have been met with the release of banknotes. As for the banknotes issued by Zhejiang Xingye, China Industrial, Siming, Tongshang, Kenye, China Agricultural and Industrial, Agricultural and Commercial, Farmers, and Zhejiang Local banks, they are all allowed to be used as usual.

Central Bank Sends Letters to Foreign Banks

In addition to sending the original text of the Ministry of Finance's public notice stating that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications were legal tender to various foreign banks, the Central Bank also sent letters requesting them to exchange silver for legal tender, stating: "The Ministry of Finance has announced a new currency system, setting several measures, including the provision that the banknotes issued by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are legal tender. At the same time, those who own silver must exchange it for legal tender. When exchanging silver, you may give legal tender to your bank, or if your bank wishes, it can be treated as a deposit. This bank is acting on this instruction and hereby notifies your bank."

Foreign Merchants Consider Measures Appropriate

Reporters from the New News Agency visited foreign banks such as Chartered Bank and HSBC yesterday morning. They all considered the Ministry of Finance's public notice stating that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications were legal tender to be an appropriate measure and the only good way to stabilize China's finances. They have all approved the Central Bank's request to exchange silver for legal tender, as this measure is very beneficial to foreign banks in China.

Banks and Money Houses Discuss Remittance Methods

The Bankers Association has decided on the second of three business methods: If there is excess remittance but a shortage of remittance heads among colleagues, silver dollars may be temporarily remitted to settle the difference with the Central Bank and the Bank of Communications. The detailed methods will be discussed jointly by the Bankers Association, the Joint Reserve of Money Houses, and the Central Bank and the Bank of Communications. According to reporters from the New News Agency, Zhu Puquan, manager of the Bankers Association's joint reserve, Qin Runqing, manager of the Money Houses' joint reserve, and representatives from the Central Bank and the Bank of Communications have already begun informally exchanging views yesterday. Once a general outline is agreed upon, a meeting will be formally convened in the coming days to decide on the methods as soon as possible to facilitate settlement between banks and money houses.

City Government Strictly Prohibits Raising Prices

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng instructed the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau yesterday, saying: "The currency policy promulgated by the Ministry of Finance this time is a major plan for the revival of the economy and the stabilization of finance, and is of utmost importance. It has been repeatedly and explicitly prohibited to attempt to speculate and raise prices. However, it has been found that commodity prices in this city have risen sharply in the past two days. For example, the price of rice has risen by as much as one or two yuan. It is obvious that unscrupulous merchants are manipulating and hoarding. If they are not severely punished, it will be insufficient to educate and deter the perpetrators and maintain local stability. In addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau to jointly and conscientiously crack down, and to arrest and prosecute unscrupulous merchants who violate the order according to the law, you are to strictly comply with this order and report the compliance situation as soon as possible. This is the order." November 5, 1935, Mayor Wu Tiecheng.

Chamber of Commerce Issues Notice Urging Restraint

To whom it may concern: The Ministry of Finance issued an order on the 4th of this month to make the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications the national legal tender. The banknotes of other Chinese banks that have been approved to issue are allowed to be used as usual. This is originally intended to centralize reserves and prevent the outflow of silver. The financial authorities have made sincere announcements to stabilize currency and finance. At the same time, a special committee has been set up to manage the issuance reserves, striving to consolidate the credibility of legal tender. All members of the business community should recognize that this move is purely to stabilize the currency system, and refrain from unnecessary disturbances. All prices for the sale of grain and food, and exchange rates for silver dollars and copper coins, should be in accordance with the Ministry of Finance's announcement on the 4th of this month, and should not be increased by more than a fraction. The price set by the Minister for money houses and the market is 12 cents of subsidiary currency or 3,000 copper coins in exchange for one yuan of legal tender, and should not be arbitrarily lowered, so as not to hinder people's livelihoods. This is of utmost importance. To the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry, Rice Shops, and Tobacco Exchange.

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: In order to stabilize currency and finance, your ministry issued a public notice on the 4th of this month making the banknotes of the three banks legal tender, and allowing the banknotes of Chinese banks that have been approved to issue to be used as usual, reviving the economy, and striving for self-reliance. The association will lead the business community to sincerely support this. However, this matter is closely related to stabilizing prices and controlling foreign exchange, and must be carried out in conjunction in order to make comprehensive plans. We request your ministry to fully plan and maintain these two aspects, and not allow those who are suspicious and speculative to obstruct and destroy, so as to live up to the original intention of reforming the currency system. We sincerely submit this request, respectfully requesting adoption. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce.

Trade Associations Jointly Telegraph Support

163 trade associations in this city, including the silk and satin industry and the paper industry, telegraphed Minister Kong, saying: "To Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance: Our country has been deeply affected by the drastic changes in silver prices. Financial crises have arisen repeatedly. Industry and commerce have declined day by day. The dangerous situation is ever-present, making it impossible to live in peace. The people have long been unable to make a living. This time, Your Excellency has taken decisive action to announce changes to the currency system, which is the only remedy to revitalize the national economy and stabilize the financial foundation. The benefits lie not only in unified issuance and centralized reserves, but also in the revival of rural areas and the development of industry and commerce. As for managing exchange rates and controlling trade, which have been limited by facts in the past and could not be decisively implemented, they can now be easily resolved. Compared to Sang Hongyang and Kong Jin, you are no less worthy. However, since the currency system is reformed, our country's economic structure will inevitably change accordingly. Prices will be stimulated first. How to equalize prices and adjust supply and demand in the future so that the national economy gradually prospers will involve a myriad of things, all related to major plans. It is believed that if we can take the opportunity to control industry and commerce and manage foreign trade to promote reasonable production and balance international receipts and payments, then the revival and salvation will lie in this move. All of the above has been previously submitted to the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce for submission to the Yuan and the Ministry, please adopt them. Your Excellency's plans for the country are impartial and loyal, and I think you have long been aware of them. Extraordinary achievements can only be accomplished by extraordinary people. I hope that you will contribute your plans and see them implemented. Our associations will certainly support your instructions with all our hearts. This telegram is submitted, respectfully requesting your review. Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry, Paper Industry, Cotton Cloth Industry, and 163 other trade associations."

Yu Qiaqing Sends Telegram Offering Opinions

Nanjing, sent separately to Chairman Jiang of the Military Commission, President Wang of the Executive Yuan, President Sun of the Legislative Yuan, President Ju of the Judicial Yuan, President Dai of the Examination Yuan, and President Yu of the Control Yuan: In recent years, the world economic panic has reached its peak. Industry and commerce have declined, and all industries have languished, especially in our country. Imports have increased year by year, and the outflow of silver has increased even more. The market for industry and commerce has declined daily. If the government authorities do not act decisively and take effective measures, the economy will inevitably collapse one day. Feeling the pain deeply, and with the national duty of a citizen, I have contributed my views to the government for the past six years, but they have not been adopted. Moreover, those engaged in finance, for the sake of maintaining their own interests, have obstructed in various ways, so that the situation has dragged on until now, with even fewer cash reserves and even tighter currency contraction. Now that the Ministry of Finance has announced the implementation of the legal tender system, although the implementation is somewhat late, it is still fortunate for the country to mend the fold after the sheep is lost. Upon hearing the news, I am deeply pleased. However, in order to seek economic recovery, we must rely on this system. As for the fundamental solution, we must at least maintain an average balance of imports and exports. To seek an average balance, maintaining and promoting industry is of the utmost importance. To revive industry, we must reduce interest rates. The excessive interest rates in our country are a fatal injury to industry. If industry can be revived, industry and commerce will naturally prosper. The Ministry of Finance's announcement has already mentioned the precedents of various countries, and sufficient funds, supply to industrial and commercial enterprises, and policies to rescue real estate have been pre-determined and will be implemented in sequence. I deeply hope that the authorities will uphold this principle and implement it resolutely, striving to realize it in the shortest possible time. We should pay more attention to construction, and construction should be based on production, and we should absolutely prevent competing with the people for profits and other malpractices. The future of revival will be somewhat promising. All of you are planning for the country, and I dare to respectfully submit my humble opinions for your adoption. Yu Hede.

Rice Market Recovers, Prices Fall Back

The rice price in this city soared the day before yesterday, and the market suddenly changed. At that time, the market price was chaotic and uneven, and the highest price broke through the peak of 13 yuan and 67 jiao. Therefore, people were panicked. After the Bean and Rice Industry Association and the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau sent personnel to earnestly persuade rice merchants from various provinces, the market situation eased slightly in the afternoon. Since yesterday, it has returned to normal. The highest rice price has fallen back by about 4 jiao, and the medium and secondary rice prices have fallen back by 7 or 8 jiao. Currently, the top-grade rice is around 13 yuan, the medium-grade rice is 12, 3, or 4 jiao, the secondary-grade rice is 11 yuan and 4 or 5 jiao, the foreign rice (Saigon) is 11 yuan and 5 jiao, and the small squeezed rice is 10 yuan and 7 or 8 jiao.

Coal Industry Association Prohibits Raising Prices

Since the Ministry of Finance issued a ban on the use of silver, some coal merchants in this city have taken the opportunity to raise the price of coal by as much as 2 or 3 yuan per ton in two days, which is obviously a monopoly. Therefore, the Coal Industry Association held an emergency executive committee meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss measures to stop this. Committee members Bao Zhezhi, Pan Yisan, Mao Chunpu, Xu Yiyong, and Han Chengpu attended. Chairman Chen Yushu reported that after the government reformed the currency system, some coal merchants raised coal prices and monopolized the market, which should be stopped. It was decided that the association would assess coal prices for sale, and those who deliberately violate this would be reported to higher authorities for severe punishment. The meeting then adjourned. The association's emergency notice is recorded below: "Emergency Notice: It has been found that coal prices have been arbitrarily raised recently. Members have reported this to the association. After convening an emergency executive committee meeting to discuss preventive measures, it was decided to notify members that at the beginning of the suspension of cash exchange, the prices of various types of coal must not be raised without reason. If there are any deliberate violations, please report to the association at any time for correction. If there are any monopolistic behaviors, the association will report the facts to higher authorities for sanctions. As for the national coal mines, they should supply as much national coal as possible and not monopolize the market and raise prices. In order to stabilize public sentiment and market prices, promote price uniformity, and promote national coal, the association hereby issues this notice for all members to comply with."

Silver Shops Have Two Questions About Business

According to reporters from the National News Agency, Fu Shengmao, standing committee member of the Silver Shops Association, said that the industry originally intended to send a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday to forward it to the Ministry of Finance to request instructions regarding the Ministry of Finance's ban on the use of silver this time. However, since this matter concerns the survival of the silver shop industry nationwide, not just a local issue in Shanghai, it is planned to solicit the opinions of silver shop colleagues across the country and then discuss the measures. Shanghai is the center, and silver shops throughout Jiangsu Province have already agreed. According to Fu, the industry has two questions regarding the Ministry of Finance's order this time: (1) If someone comes to exchange old jewelry in the future, should it be accepted? Accepting it would violate the Ministry of Finance's order, and refusing it would cause a shortage of raw materials. (2) Currently, each silver shop still has a small amount of silver that can be used for utensils, but after it is used up, there will be a shortage of raw materials. Can the Central Bank supply it continuously? Otherwise, the silver shop industry nationwide will not be able to survive. It is hoped that the government will pay attention to the above two points.

Public Works Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses the Matter of Telephone Rate Hikes 63

Chinese and Foreign Committee Members Consider Each Clause in Detail; Experts from Four Countries Attend and Respond

Following the submission of the report on telephone issues by the Special Telephone Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council to the Board of Directors, the Public Works Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council convened a meeting on Monday (October 28th) to discuss telephone matters. Various experts attended to provide consultations. The experts present included Mr. Hu Ruixiang (Chinese), Mr. Inada (Japanese), Mr. Brown (British), and Mr. Ray (American). Members of the Public Works Committee first inquired of the experts whether the prevailing state of general socio-economic decline had been taken into consideration when formulating the various recommendations. Expert Mr. Brown responded that while this point was not discussed at the beginning of the report, the final recommendations were not entirely unrelated to the current economic situation. A member of the Public Works Committee stated that the report did not elaborate on how prices should be increased if the Shanghai Municipal Council decided to retain the per-instrument billing method, and therefore, the report was not yet complete. Mr. Brown replied that this question was very simple. From April 1st to the end of July, the net profit of the Shanghai Telephone Company had almost reached 10 percent. However, if the per-instrument charge was increased by another 11 percent to offset the losses from the reduction in the number of telephones, the company could obtain a net profit of 10 percent. Mr. Ray added that if the existing per-instrument charge were increased again to achieve the desired net profit, the number of telephones would inevitably decrease further. If so, the telephone rates would inevitably increase again. Therefore, even under the per-instrument system, there was no reliable method for ensuring the company's revenue. Subsequently, upon the recommendation of various committee members and with the agreement of the experts, an appendix was added to the report, outlining the pricing that should be adopted if the per-instrument system were to be retained.

The discussion then moved on to the "Equipment" section of the report. Mr. Brown stated that he had personally visited fifty or sixty telephone users, and Mr. Ray also stated that he had spoken with twenty or thirty users. They all stated that the current service was far superior to what they had previously had. Mr. Brown stated that he had not been able to speak with a large number of Japanese users, but based on the results of his conversations with a small number of Japanese people, he could conclude that public opinion must be highly satisfied. Mr. Inada stated that he had met with a large number of Japanese people, and they all said that the telephone service was excellent, but some of them had raised various difficulties in communicating with the Chinese areas.

When discussing the expenditure section, the item "intangible capital of over 30,000 yuan" was mentioned. It was said that this item came from the old company's old accounts, representing the price paid for assets and the difference between the subsequent price adjustment. Moreover, since the conversion to automatic switchboards, capital expenditures for business expansion had already increased. Mr. Brown stated that the total amount of the company's expenditure was approximately 40 million yuan, which was the estimated value of all the company's assets in 1934, including those acquired from the old company and those added independently, up to that time. As stated in the report, the various properties were listed and then constituted the total amount of the company's investment. After the replacement of automatic switchboards, the clearing procedures were cumbersome and had to be somewhat delayed, so a comprehensive estimate was only available by July 1934. Mr. Ray added that this 40 million yuan was, first, the result of the estimated value of the old company's equipment in 1934. This estimate was made on August 5, 1930. The remainder was the cost of new equipment and properties built since 1930. In other words, the old properties in use, combined with the new properties built since 1930, equaled 40 million yuan.

A committee member immediately inquired about how depreciation was handled between 1930 and 1934. Mr. Brown said that, according to the practices of all other telephone companies, in order to maintain the integrity of capital, a depreciation rate must be found on all property. The method of seeking this rate must be carried out step by step in each department. That is, the length of life of each part of the equipment must first be determined, and then multiplied by the amount of investment in each part. This percentage, if applied to all of the telephone company's equipment, would reach 4.5 percent per year. Regardless of the company, this depreciation percentage should be set aside as amortization of the company's assets. Mr. Brown continued that this method of depreciation calculation is beneficial to both the company and its users, because the company's net profit is enjoyed not on 40 million, but on 34 million yuan of invested capital.

Continuing to discuss the equipment installation at each station, a committee member inquired whether the rapid completion of the automatic switchboard replacement work had any effect on the final cost. Mr. Brown said that this question was quite difficult to answer, because it contained components of comparison that should be weighed. On the one hand, in order to ensure that the work was scientific, fifty engineers were brought in from all over the world to specialize in the matter, and the cost would inevitably increase. But at the same time, because of the use of these top-notch professionals, the work was completed on time, and the period during which all personnel should be paid was shortened. Roughly speaking, seeking rapid and complete work would inevitably lead to a slight increase in costs, but it was impossible to make a definitive conclusion. A committee member further inquired whether it was an unreasonable requirement for the automatic switchboard conversion work to be completed within two years. Mr. Brown said that there was nothing unreasonable about it.

Regarding the exchange rate, a committee member inquired how the company prevented losses from exchange rate fluctuations. The head of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Finance Department replied that the company had settled its foreign exchange at appropriate exchange rates and times, so from a global perspective, telephone users need not worry too much about this.

The committee members then discussed the company's operating and maintenance expenses. According to the experts' opinions, these equipment expenses could not be reduced unless they could be obtained from China or locations closer than the existing ones. As for the report's statement that the total cost of each telephone in Shanghai was 46.2 yuan, with what was it being compared? Mr. Brown said that comparable costs included China's 35 yuan per telephone and Japan's 37 yuan. However, in Shanghai, there were other reasons for the increased expenditure, most of which were listed in the report. At this point, a committee member pointed out that the number of foreign employees enjoying high salaries in the company was an important reason. However, without these high-salaried foreign employees, foreign investment would not be so enthusiastic. Mr. Ray stated that only companies under the same jurisdiction with equivalent standards could be appropriately compared. Therefore, in the United States, a price adopted in one place was often rejected by the courts in another. Mr. Brown also said that telephone construction in the United Kingdom and the United States had its own differences, so it was unfair to compare them rashly. However, in terms of the situation in Shanghai, the cost of supply was not too high.

Regarding the per-call charging system, Mr. Brown said that he had received hundreds of letters on the subject. In his view, most of them originated from people who abused the telephone. He had personally investigated and discovered many abuses. This abuse was the reason why the per-instrument charging system had been abandoned everywhere in the world. More than a decade ago, the British House of Commons also discussed this matter. According to the report of the House of Commons committee, only a small number of users who "made the most of" the telephone at the time advocated for retaining the per-instrument charging system. The so-called "use" was actually "abuse." Therefore, the special committee deeply wished to prevent users from paying only the monthly rent for the per-instrument charge while making more than 2,000 calls per month. However, as stated in the report, more than half of residential users would pay lower telephone bills in the future. Mr. Ray also stated that under the current per-instrument charging system, the company's revenue came entirely from small users, while the company lost money on large users. Therefore, part of what small users paid was the price for the enjoyment of the use of the telephone by other users. Furthermore, if the per-instrument charge were increased again, the number of telephones would inevitably decrease, and the effectiveness of the supply would not diminish as a result. This was detrimental to all aspects of Shanghai's economic society. If a per-call charging price was adopted, small users would benefit first, and the number of people subscribing to the telephone would also increase, gradually making the function more widespread. This was the simplest philosophy of the per-call charging system.

A committee member then stated that although it was said that general small users could save on telephone bills in the future, most still favored the per-instrument charging system because it was easier to control revenue when the per-instrument charging system was used. Since the company had agreed to obtain a profit of 13 percent, it could settle for a profit of no more than 10 percent and no less than 10 percent under the existing system.

Mr. Brown said that when the Special Telephone Committee discussed the reduction in the number of calls, it did not say that 37.5 percent was an exact and unchangeable number. This number was merely the average of the 50 percent reduction rate in Japan and the 25 percent reduction rate in the United Kingdom. However, at that time, the number of calls in the United Kingdom was not very high, so the impact after changing to the per-call charging system was small. Currently, Shanghai telephone users make a very high number of calls, so the reduction component in the future is extremely large. The extent of the future reduction will inevitably exceed 25 percent, or even reach 37.5 percent. Mr. Brown also said that the profit earned on the Shanghai Telephone Company's investment was not beyond the norm. The Copenhagen Telephone Company in Denmark had previously enjoyed an equivalent profit for as long as twenty years. The net profit earned annually by the various companies of the American Bell System was also consistently between eight and nine percent. Mr. Brown also said that the per-instrument charging system was absolutely unfair and caused many abuses. Furthermore, according to the experts, if the company's profit were to exceed one point in the future, the telephone charges could still be required to be reduced. Currently, because of the desire to adopt the per-call charging system, the number can only be approximate. On this point, it cannot be as accurate as under the per-instrument charging system. However, in view of the above reasons, this point is not important. But if the per-instrument charging system must still be used in the future, then the authorities will inevitably have to face an extremely large expenditure. At that time, it may be necessary to add a central switchboard with a capital of 30,000 yuan to meet the needs of a very high number of calls. The current equipment in the central area of the telephone company is sufficient to supply 10,000 users under normal conditions. However, due to the very high number of calls, there are many places where the supply is lacking. If the number of calls does not return to normal in the near future and the economic situation gradually improves, the company will have to add equipment for 10,000 lines in the business area.

The chairman then summarized the opinions of the various committee members and experts as follows: the company's revenue is easier to calculate under the per-instrument charging system than under the per-call charging system. However, the Telephone Special Committee felt that even under the per-call charging system, the calculation would not be very different. The committee members also felt that the benefits of the per-call charging system were more than enough to cover this concern, making it a truly viable option. The chairman reminded the committee members that before the experts came to Shanghai, the Shanghai Telephone Company, in its consultation with the Shanghai Municipal Council, had agreed that after the per-call charging system was implemented in the future, it would be willing to include the excess revenue earned in the telephone price revision account within one year. This plan could still be put forward to the company in the future, stipulating a trial period. It was expected that the company would not overturn the original agreement under the same conditions.

Afterwards, a committee member inquired about the reliability of the call counters. Mr. Brown said that among the various simple and indestructible mechanical structures, the telephone call counter was one of the most reliable. Chinese expert Mr. Hu Ruixiang further explained the content of this mechanical work and said that this machine only recorded the number of completed calls. According to Mr. Brown, the current average number of calls per day for Shanghai users is 11 for residential users and 18 for business users. He also said that after the implementation of the new system, 50 percent of business users and 59 percent of residential users would benefit as a result.

Regarding the fact that the current proposed per-call charging system is calculated based on the company's net profit of 8.54 percent, a committee member raised the clause in the concession contract that the company still has the right to include the shortfall in the telephone fee revision account. Mr. Brown said that all the experts were aware of this point.

The head of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Finance Department observed that after the implementation of the new system, the profit on the company's invested capital would be approximately 8.58 percent, and the shortfall would be included in the telephone fee revision item. However, the company would have many opportunities to improve in the future, so that the profit could be increased to 10 percent. When this goal could be achieved would depend entirely on future circumstances. Mr. Ray explained that if the number of telephones did not increase in the future, the company's profit might only reach 8 percent. However, if the number of telephones increased as expected, the company's profit would also be greater.

A committee member further inquired whether the installed telephone lines could be used for unlimited calls without restrictions. Mr. Brown said that was not the case. The monthly rental for the first line was 10 yuan, and the monthly fee for the second and subsequent lines was 5 yuan, without any included number of calls. Therefore, whether on the first line or on the other branch lines, only 150 calls could be made free of charge, and all others would be charged according to the number of calls.

The meeting came to an end at this point, and it was decided to reopen on November 7th. The meeting was then adjourned.

Second Special District Federation Opposes Per-Call Telephone Billing 64

Sends Another Letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council Requesting Measures to Prevent It; Otherwise, Refuse to Pay and Let Them Remove the Telephone

The Second Special District Citizens' Federation, regarding the telephone company's change in billing method to per-call billing, which citizens have expressed opposition to, had previously sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council requesting them to prevent it, but had not received a reply. Yesterday, they sent another letter to the Council, requesting them to immediately take measures to prevent it. A reporter from the New New News Agency has extracted the original letter as follows: Dear Sirs, regarding the issue of the Shanghai Telephone Company's price increase, our Federation had previously sent a letter to your Council requesting you to take measures to prevent it. Now we understand that the Telephone Expert Committee has completed its review, and its report has admitted that the Shanghai Telephone Company should obtain a net profit of 10 percent in fulfilling its franchise contract, and its billing method is that commercial telephones will be charged 10 yuan per month for 150 calls, and household telephones will be charged 6.5 yuan per month for 100 calls, and an additional 3 cents will be charged for each additional call. If calculated according to this number, commercial telephones are limited to 150 calls per month, with an average of only five calls per day, and household telephones are limited to 100 calls per month, with an average of less than four calls per day. However, how many more than five or four times a day are commercial and household telephones used? If the price is doubled, how much will the price increase be? If the price is tripled, how much will the price increase be? The economy is currently depressed, so how can people bear this heavy burden? Furthermore, the company's restriction on calls is so strict that if commercial and household users remove their telephones due to the low utility, or only keep one of two telephones, or use two-cent postage for communication, or take other measures because they cannot afford to exceed five or four times a day by several times, may we ask how the company will obtain a net profit of 10 percent? The Expert Committee has not taken this into account and has insisted on maintaining the company's 10 percent net profit as a prerequisite, and the company is only concerned about its own generous annual interest and does not consider whether users can afford it, acting stubbornly and without any relaxation. Our Federation, representing the citizens of the entire district, cannot agree to this plan in any way. If the company must implement per-call billing, then all users will have to refuse to pay and let them remove the telephones. As this matter concerns social welfare, we are sending another letter to your Council, requesting you to consider the public opinion of the citizens and not implement this per-call billing method in any way, so as to stabilize society and comply with public opinion.

Self-Produced, Self-Used Rent Should Also Be Reduced at This Time 67

Taxpayers Association Sends Another Letter to Shanghai Municipal Council on Behalf of China-France Pharmacy

The Shanghai Taxpayers Association of the Chinese Concession sent a letter to the Acting General Manager of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession yesterday, stating: Dear Sirs, regarding the donation case of the China-France Pharmacy Co., Ltd., after receiving your Council's reply B535 of October 16, we immediately forwarded it to the company. Now, according to their reply of October 29, we would like to draw your Council's attention to the following facts: (1) When general rents are high, the rent for self-produced and self-used properties can be estimated high. Conversely, when general rents are low, the rent for self-produced and self-used properties should be reduced. (2) All rent reductions are notified to the Shanghai Taxpayers Association or directly to the Municipal Council by letter in accordance with the law, and the total amount of donation is reduced accordingly. (3) The Cotton Mill Association has requested the Taxpayers Association to forward a letter to the Municipal Council to reduce the estimated rent. (4) There is also a court judgment reducing rent by 20 percent, as seen in various newspapers. (5) Our office has paid the total donation in accordance with the law for the reasonable amount of rent, but it has been rejected by the Donation Office. Based on the above reasons, the pharmacy does not change its previous claims, but does not neglect the opportunity for a truly independent and legally based rent valuation. We are sending this letter to your Council for handling.

Rampant Bandits in Zhejiang Sea Fishing Area: Fishermen Telegraph Shanghai for Help 68

More Than Twenty Fishing Boats Looted: Request for Patrol Ships to Rescue

The Shenjiamen Fishery Association of Zhejiang and other fishermen's organizations sent a telegram to the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Industry's Fishery Protection Bureau yesterday, stating that piracy is rampant during the fishing season, with a large number of fishing boats being looted, making it extremely urgent to send patrol ships to protect the fishing grounds and simultaneously dispatch troops to directly attack the bandit hideouts and rescue the fishermen in distress. The association recently received reports from fishermen that on the afternoon of October 21st, more than twenty pairs of fishing boats, including those of Zhang Xiaoniang, Chen Qingtang, Jiang Axiao, Bei Fusheng, Xia Dingxing, and Xin Yunqing, were looted by bandits in the Guanshan sea area. Both the people and boats were kidnapped, and the fishing gear was completely devastated. The bandit leader, Jin Shunan, Huang Chunshan, threatened that after receiving the message, they must go to the designated location to negotiate ransom, otherwise the boats would be destroyed and the hostages killed. Their rampant and stubborn wickedness is such as this. According to the association's report, there are no patrol ships in the fishing area and no ships to pursue the bandits on the spot. Public security on the water is full of difficulties, and fishermen's livelihoods are becoming more and more difficult. This year, the money spent on going to sea for boat pairs, purchasing tools, and all the costs of the boats are entirely from pawning possessions. They are doing it reluctantly, only wanting to seek enough food and clothing for their families amidst difficulties. If the fishing area is where bandits can be encountered everywhere, then the families of the victims are crying to the heavens and the rest of the boat pairs are in imminent danger. Therefore, we urgently request that patrol ships be dispatched quickly to the fishing area to provide effective patrols. At the same time, send troops to pursue and suppress the bandits and rescue the distressed people.

Patrol Ship Sinks Pirate Ship Outside Wusong Estuary 73

Many Bandits Captured with Gunshot Wounds

The day before yesterday morning, a Gonghemao fishing boat was robbed outside the Wusong estuary of the Huangpu River. A customs patrol ship happened to be patrolling nearby and, upon learning of the robbery, immediately warned the bandits on board. The boat did not stop or surrender and resisted arrest. The patrol ship then fired on the boat, sinking it on the spot. Many bandits were captured, including Gong Fangfu from Ningbo, 35 years old, who suffered a gunshot wound to his right leg. He was immediately handed over to the Lujiazui Water Patrol Police Station, where Patrol Officer No. 92 sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment and assigned an officer to guard him. Impoverished and Unable to Afford Medical Treatment: Tragic Suicide of a Woman by Slitting Her Throat; Severed Blood Vessels, Profuse Bleeding, Ineffective Treatment, Death 75

Xu, née Xu, a 36-year-old woman from Shaoxing, residing at No. 153 Zhaoyang Road, Pudong, had a husband, Xu Changtai, who made a meager living selling newspapers. They had four children, all young, making life extremely difficult. Unexpectedly, Mrs. Xu suddenly fell ill a decade ago, but they could not afford medical treatment. Her condition worsened in recent days, and she could not get out of bed. In this situation, she was resentful and conceived the idea of ending her life. Taking advantage of the absence of her husband and children by her bedside, she grabbed a kitchen knife and stabbed herself in the neck. The blood vessels were severed, and she bled profusely. After her husband and others discovered her, they rushed her to the hospital, but the treatment was ineffective, and she soon died. The Yangshupu Police Station was notified and dispatched an officer to investigate. The body was taken to the Phalen Road morgue for examination. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue. After examining the body and questioning her husband, Xu Changtai, about the circumstances, Guo determined that the deceased Xu, née Xu, a woman, had indeed committed suicide by slitting her throat. The body was handed over to her husband, Xu Changtai, to claim for burial after signing an affidavit.

Municipal Finance Bureau to Collect Winter House Tax 76

Starting November 5th

Since the Municipal Finance Bureau improved the collection method of house tax in the urban area, households with tax amounts of more than ten yuan are encouraged to go to the tax collection offices to pay, and the response has been enthusiastic. The bureau issued a notice yesterday, announcing that the collection of this year's winter house tax will begin on November 5th. For areas far from the tax collection offices, such as the Wusong district, house tax payments can be made at the Wusong City Ferry Terminal vehicle tax office. For the Jiangwan district, house tax payments can be made directly to the Jiangwan Land Tax Collection Office to provide convenience. The Municipal Finance Bureau's announcement on the collection of winter house tax is as follows: Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Announcement No. 313: It is hereby announced that the method of improving the collection of house tax in the urban area has been announced by this bureau. It is hereby announced that the collection of this winter's commissioned house tax will begin on November 5th. For those with tax amounts of more than ten yuan, each tax collection office of this bureau will issue a notice at the beginning of the collection period, requiring the taxpayer to pay at the office within fifteen days. If the payment is delayed by more than ten days, staff will be sent to collect the tax at the door, and a fine of 2% of the tax amount will be added to deter procrastination. Those with tax amounts of less than ten yuan will still have staff sent to collect. Those who voluntarily pay at the office are welcome. In addition to instructing each tax collection office to comply, this announcement is made for general knowledge. This announcement is dated November of the 24th year of the Republic of China. Director Cai Zengji.

Check Bounced Despite Funds in Bank 79

Sheng Zhiren Sues Xi Hanying for Damage to Credit

Sheng Zhiren, a resident of No. 8 Dingji Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, a member of the former French Concession Business Association, and a native of Changzhou, deposited funds in the name of Zhi Ji into the China Bank Baxianqiao Branch on Rue Cardinal Mercier, French Concession, and has been doing so for six years. As of the end of July this year, Sheng's deposit balance was 120 yuan. On August 3rd, he deposited 190 yuan and paid out 163 yuan, leaving a balance of 147 yuan. The next day (August 4th), Sheng issued a check for 104 yuan to another person, who then transferred it to the Shanghai Bank for collection. However, Xi Hanying, the accounting director of the China Bank Baxianqiao Branch, a native of Suzhou, had a grudge against Sheng and refused to pay the check, bouncing it. The next day, when the check was presented again, it was still rejected. Xi even wrote "Come tomorrow to collect the numbers" on the returned check slip. Sheng Zhiren believed that the amount of the deposit exceeded the amount of the check and that the procedures were complete. He suspected that Xi Hanying deliberately made things difficult. After going to the bank to lodge a complaint, he was able to cash the check. Sheng, as a businessman, regards credit as the only essential element of business. His deposit exceeded the amount of the check, yet it was unjustly bounced and refused to be cashed, which he believed was a deliberate attempt to damage his reputation. Feeling aggrieved, he filed a private prosecution with the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court, accusing Xi Hanying of the crime of damaging credit under Article 313 of the new Criminal Code, requesting the court to investigate and prosecute him according to law, and attaching a civil lawsuit requesting the court to order the defendant to publish an apology advertisement to restore his reputation. The court accepted the case and heard it in the Second Criminal Court at 11:00 yesterday morning, presided over by Judge Sun Pengham. The defendant did not appear, only the plaintiff Sheng Zhiren was present. After briefly questioning his age and origin, the court informed the plaintiff that the subpoena for the defendant Xi Hanying had not yet been served. According to the bailiff's report, the bank stated that the defendant had resigned. Sheng was also unaware of the defendant's address and suspected that he had been transferred to the head office. The court also stated that the legal article cited by the plaintiff in the complaint did not correspond to the facts and ordered him to correct it immediately, and ordered a 15-day adjournment, ordering the plaintiff to summon the defendant for further questioning.

Unfortunate Incident Occurs While Young Girl Left Alone in Shanghai 80

Hu Jinmei Unable to Resist Li Jiagen's Inhumanity

Hu Jinmei, a girl from Jiangbei, is 17 years old and lives at No. 1021 Binlang Road, West Shanghai. She works as a factory worker at the Japanese-owned Naigaiwata No. 13 Factory on Robison Road. A few days ago, Hu was engaged to Yuan Jiasheng, a worker at the Peicheng Sock Factory on Seymour Road, through a matchmaker. However, Hu's elder sister had already been promised to a man surnamed Mou from their Jiangbei hometown, and the wedding was scheduled to take place within days. Therefore, Hu's parents and sisters returned to their hometown together the day before yesterday to prepare everything, leaving only Hu Jinmei alone to look after the house in Shanghai. When Hu's parents left, because Jinmei was young and inexperienced, they instructed Jinmei's fiancé, Yuan Jiasheng, to take care of her. Unexpectedly, Li Jiagen, a man from Anhui (also known as Li Changgen, 43 years old), residing at No. 6 Xiaoshadu Road, who was acquainted with the Hu family, broke into the Hu's house alone at around 7:00 in the morning the day before yesterday. At that time, Hu Jinmei had just returned home from working the night shift, having finished work at 6:00 in the morning, and was preparing to sleep. Seeing Li's arrival, she greeted him. After some conversation, Li learned that Hu's entire family had returned to their hometown, leaving only Jinmei alone in the house. He had bad intentions and went out to buy a few pieces of Cifan (a type of glutinous rice snack) and copper coins, asking Jinmei to eat them and coaxing her with sweet words. He then closed the door and forcibly pushed Hu Jinmei onto the bed, covering her head with a quilt to prevent her from making a sound, and committed indecent assault. Hu was helpless and alone, and under the force of violence, she was unable to resist and was ravaged. At around 8:00, her fiancé, Yuan Jiasheng, and the matchmaker, Zhang Yuancai, went to visit her and saw that the door was tightly closed. They knocked on the door. At that time, Li Jiagen and Hu were fast asleep. Suddenly hearing the knock, they were shocked. Li climbed out of the window and onto the cabinet outside the window, hoping to escape. Suddenly, the second landlord, Jin Qiangen, saw him and suspected that he was a thief, so he shouted loudly. Neighbors gathered. Seeing that the situation was not good, Li turned around and fled back into Hu's room. By this time, Hu had opened the door, and Li was seized by Yuan and others, twisted over to Chinese patrol, and taken to the Gordon Road Police Station. Under the questioning of Chinese detective Zhang Liang, Hu, out of shame, did not reveal the truth, so the detectives initially did not know the real story. Li, on the other hand, accused Yuan of stealing his hat. Later, after questioning by Chinese and Western detectives, Hu Jinmei confessed to the ordeal she had suffered. The police then searched Hu's house and found stained trousers and two bed sheets, which they took back to the police station. They sent Hu to Guangren Hospital, where it was confirmed that her hymen had been broken. They ordered Li to be detained and transferred to the Criminal Division of the First Special Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin prosecuted him under Article 221 of the Criminal Code and presented the case. Judge Liu Yugui declared that the case concerned morality and prohibited spectators from attending. As a result, Judge Liu declared the debate closed and scheduled the sentencing for the morning of the 7th of this month.

Sun Fucai Sentenced for Damaging Mother's Corpse 81

Sentenced to Two Years Imprisonment

Sun Jinshi, an elderly woman from Ningbo, 58 years old, came to Shanghai with her son, Fucai (30 years old), on September 14th, staying at the home of her son-in-law, Xin Xingkuan, No. 89 McCot Road, to find business opportunities for her son. However, there were no suitable jobs. Later, the mother suddenly fell ill and became increasingly ill, but the Xin family was unable to afford medical treatment and only prayed to Buddha and took herbal remedies. Unexpectedly, she died at 5:00 pm on the 27th of last month. Sun Fucai was furious and took advantage of the opportunity to use a knife to stab a hole in his mother's abdomen. He reported to the Hongkou Police Station, saying that his mother had been murdered by her brother-in-law, Xin Xingkuan, and stabbed to death, demanding justice. After the case was filed, Chinese Detective Chief Zhu Jihuang and Detective Zi Baimingfu escorted him to the First Special District Court. Sun Jinshi's body was clearly examined by the prosecutor and forensic doctor, confirming that she had died of illness. Sun Fucai's interrogation and detention have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department stated that there was a witness who could prove the situation after Sun Jinshi's death and that the defendant had falsely accused Xin Xingkuan, etc. According to his nephew, Xin Fuquan, after Sun Jinshi's death, the defendant came with four friends and took the opportunity to make trouble, accusing his uncle of murder, etc. According to Yong woman Jiang Ye, who worked as a servant in the Xu family, relatives of Xin, after Sun Jinshi's death, she went to the Xin family to help and washed the body with hot water, and there was no knife wound or hole in the abdomen. At that time, the defendant was also watching clearly, etc. When questioned, the defendant still stammered in his confession. Judge Jiang ruled that Sun Fucai was guilty of damaging the corpse of a direct blood relative and sentenced him to two years of imprisonment.

Lawyers Association Requests Investigation into the Removal of Written Records 86

Shen Yuankai Suspected of Destroying Evidence

The Shanghai Lawyers Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Judicial Administration yesterday, stating that it was submitting a report from Yuan Sunpinlian, reporting that Cheng Shen Yuankai, trial officer of the Qingpu County Government, had suppressed evidence and requesting a thorough investigation. According to the letter from Yuan Sunpinlian of Lupu, he filed a lawsuit with the Jiangsu Qingpu County Government against Sun Chuanhui for the analysis of the inheritance, and was sentenced in September of the 23rd year. Yuan appealed to the High Court because he did not accept the original judgment. However, on March 4th of this year, during the second hearing in the High Court, it was discovered that the file of the Qingpu County Government regarding this case was missing a written record of the court hearing on April 27th of the 23rd year, claiming that neither the plaintiff nor the defendant were present in court on that day. The attorney for Mr. Chen, Attorney Chen, told the presiding judge that "When the Qingpu County Government heard this case on that day, the husband of a person from the asylum attended and took notes. This is a fact that cannot be ignored and was removed by the trial officer because he saw testimony that was unfavorable to the person from the asylum." And asked the clerk to record this matter in the court hearing record. The importance of the record lies in the testimony of Xu Shenhou, the witness presented by Sun Chuanhui. Xu only attended court once in this case, which was on April 27th of the 23rd year. Trial officer Shen Zushou was transferred to Taicang and succeeded by Shen Yuankai. Therefore, it is necessary to distinguish who removed the record. After detailed research, it was discovered that the person who removed the record was actually Shen Yuankai. (Omitted) There is also a judgment from the Qingpu County Government as proof. This kind of suppression of evidence, dereliction of duty and perversion of the law, and the destruction of official documents are incompatible with the spirit of the rule of law and cannot be tolerated by today's movement to rectify official discipline. In addition to filing a complaint with the Ministry of Judicial Administration, I am humbly seeking your association's assistance to present this matter to a meeting and request the Jiangsu High Court to transfer Shen Yuankai for disciplinary action and dismissal. After the association submitted the matter to a joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committee, it was resolved to submit it to your ministry for thorough investigation.

Unresolved Wang Yaochen Estate Dispute: Lu Xingyuan Sues Qiu Hanping 88

Accusations of False Accusation, Incitement to False Accusation, and Defamation: The First Special Court Summoned Lu Yesterday for Preliminary Hearing

Wang Yaochen, also known as Wang Yousu, a native of Xiamen, Fujian, who held dual nationality by retaining his original nationality while registering as a French citizen, passed away on November 18th of last year at his residence, No. 7, Yugu Village, Yuyuan Road, in this city. During his final illness, he specifically requested lawyer Lu Xingyuan to come to his home and sign a will at his bedside, entrusting it to his concubine, Du Ruizhen, for safekeeping. He also asked his friend, Shi Zhinan (also known as Shi Yuankai), who was then serving as an assistant at the Salt Revenue Audit Office, to be the executor of the will. After his death, his wife from his ancestral home, Ouyang Shunying, along with his son Wang Shengduan, published a statement in the newspaper declaring that all of Wang Yaochen's

Property in Shanghai and Xiamen

was to be inherited by his wife and son. Anyone with objections was to provide evidence within two weeks. However, Du Ruizhen did not respond to Ouyang's statement at the time. It was not until March 17th of this year that she instructed her nephew, Wang Sheng, to send a letter to the French Consulate in Xiamen requesting the registration of Wang Yaochen's will so that she could inherit all of Yaochen's estate. When Ouyang learned of this, she vehemently opposed it, and the French Consulate did not

Approve the Registration, leading to Litigation between the two parties in the Xiamen

Courts.

However, Du soon mortgaged and sold the land on Route Tenant de Béhaine in the French Concession of this city, which further aroused Ouyang's resentment. Last month, she hired lawyer Qiu Hanping to file a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Court against Du Ruizhen, Lu Xingyuan, Shi Zhinan, and others, alleging that the will was a forgery concocted by Du and the others. Du Ruizhen was accused of violating Articles 210, 216, 217, and 320, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code, Lu Xingyuan was accused of violating Articles 210, 217, and 215 of the Criminal Code, and Shi Zhinan was accused of violating Article 30 of the Criminal Code, requesting

Legal Punishment

and ordering the return of the stolen and sold land. The First Special Court has already conducted two preliminary hearings involving Lu and Shi. Lu and Shi, arguing that Ouyang Shunying should not have sued them, also filed a counterclaim for false accusation. The presiding judge, Mr. Xiao Fen, ordered a postponement, stating that an investigation was needed from the Xiamen District Court, and further questioning would be conducted upon the Xiamen Court's response, as previously reported in detail. It has now been learned that, in addition to joining Shi Zhinan in counter-suing

Ouyang Shunying

for false accusation in that case, lawyer Lu Xingyuan has now independently filed a criminal self-accusation against lawyer Qiu Hanping, who drafted the complaint for Ouyang, on three counts: (1) false accusation, (2) incitement to false accusation, and (3) defamation. Judge Wu Zehan of the First Special Court, who is handling the case, summoned the plaintiff, Lu Xingyuan, to court yesterday afternoon for a preliminary hearing to understand the meaning of his accusations. According to Lu's statement, the false accusation he accused Qiu Hanping of was based on Qiu's report to the Jing'an Temple Police Station on September 3rd, on behalf of Ouyang Shunying, accusing us of conspiring to

Forge a Will.

He accused him of inciting false accusation because the complaint filed by Wang Ouyang Shunying against Du Ruizhen, me, and Shi Zhinan for forging private documents was drafted by Qiu Hanping. The reason for accusing him of defamation was that Qiu should not have disclosed the drafted complaint to newspapers. When the case of Ouyang's self-accusation of forging private documents was heard, Ouyang stated the facts of the prosecution in court but did not mention the legal articles under which the defendant was accused. However, the next day, various newspapers carried

Reports of the Hearing

detailing each defendant's alleged violations of the law, which were completely identical to those described in the original complaint, indicating that Qiu Hanping had leaked the complaint. The fact that Wang Yaochen signed the will had previously been testified to in court by Shi Zhinan and witnesses. Therefore, Ouyang's false accusation will certainly be substantiated in the future, he said. He then presented newspapers, judgments from the Xiamen court, and photos of Wang Yaochen's handwriting as evidence, claiming that they were all sufficient to prove that the signature on the will was indeed Wang's. After examining the evidence, Judge Wu ordered a postponement to the afternoon of November 19th for further questioning.

Chen Baochen's Coffin Transported to Shanghai; Public Memorial Service at China Merchants Wharf 94

Chen Baochen, former tutor of the Xuantong Emperor of the Qing Dynasty, passed away in Beijing this spring at the age of 88. His coffin was transported from Beijing to Tianjin on the 3rd of this month and then transferred to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming Wheel to travel south. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 8th and will be temporarily placed in the warehouse at the New Kaihe China Merchants Wharf for one or two days. At that time, his relatives and friends in Shanghai plan to hold a public memorial service. His eldest son, Jishi, second son, Yuanshi, third son, Zhizi, and daughters-in-law are all traveling south with the coffin. The arrangements in Shanghai are currently being handled by Chen's seventh son-in-law, He Yunming, and ninth son-in-law, Zhang Zimei, who reside in Shanghai. After the coffin arrives in Minjiang, the family will follow Chen's wishes and avoid extravagance. After holding a family and public memorial service, they will choose a date for burial.

Strict Ban on Opium and Drugs on the Seas; Crew Members Must Obtain Joint Guarantees 95

Guarantees Must Be Completed Within Two Months; One Person's Crime, Three People Punished

The central government is strictly enforcing the prohibition of opium and drugs. All employees of various ships are required to obtain a three-person joint guarantee to prevent the smuggling of drugs and the provision of opium for smoking. This has now been announced in Shanghai. The Shanghai Marine Engineer's Union has copied and distributed the guarantee rules to all crew members for compliance. The original letter is transcribed as follows: "Greetings, we have received a letter from Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, stating that the members Ning Shaosan, Beida Xing, and other companies have reported that they have received a dispatch from the Administrative Inspector of the Ning County Administrative Inspectorate District of Zhejiang Province, along with the Regulations on Joint Guarantees to Strictly Prohibit the Transportation and Provision of Opium and Drugs by Crew Members of Various Ships in Zhejiang Province, and a sample of the Joint Guarantee Pledge, instructing all ships to comply. Prohibition of opium must be complied with. In addition to instructing the crew members of each ship to comply with the joint guarantee rules, there may be misunderstandings among the crew members due to a lack of understanding of the facts. We request that the union forward a letter to the various maritime groups for simultaneous assistance to facilitate progress and avoid violations of orders. Previously, the Regulations on Joint Guarantees to Strictly Prohibit the Transportation and Provision of Opium and Drugs by Crew Members of Various Ships in Zhejiang Province have been submitted to the Chairman of the Military Commission and Superintendent General of Opium Suppression for approval and implementation, which should be complied with. In response to the previous situation, we have enclosed a copy of the joint guarantee rules and a sample of the pledge for your reference and forwarding to the relevant members for compliance, etc. We have also included a copy of the joint guarantee rules and a sample of the pledge. In response to this, the transportation and provision of opium and drugs are strictly prohibited by national law. These joint guarantee rules must be complied with. We have issued a copy of the joint guarantee rules and three copies of the joint guarantee pledge and request that your members promptly find joint guarantors, fill them out, and submit them to the association for submission to the central management agency for filing. (Regulations on Joint Guarantees to Strictly Prohibit the Transportation and Provision of Opium and Drugs by Crew Members of Various Ships in Zhejiang Province (Article 1) In order to strictly prohibit the transportation or provision of opium and drugs in this province, these Regulations on Joint Guarantees to Strictly Prohibit the Transportation and Provision of Opium and Drugs by Crew Members of Various Ships are specifically formulated. All ships shall order all crew members to comply. (Article 2) All crew members of each ship shall jointly associate in groups of three and shall not transport or provide lamps for smoking opium and drugs. If any member of the joint guarantee is found to be transporting or providing opium and drugs on the ship and it is confirmed, if the perpetrator escapes, the co-guarantors shall be responsible for handing over the person. Each crew member may only join one joint guarantee. All guarantors shall be employees of similar rank, and if there are not three employees of similar rank, adjustments may be made according to the circumstances. (Article 3) If a guarantor knows that any member of the joint guarantee is transporting or providing lamps for smoking opium and drugs, they shall secretly report it in a timely manner. If the report is confirmed to be true, the reporting person shall be exempt from liability and shall find another joint guarantee. (Article 4) If any member of the joint guarantee suspects that a guarantor is transporting or providing lamps for smoking opium and drugs, they may state their withdrawal from the guarantee at any time. After withdrawal, the original guarantor shall find another joint guarantee within ten days. (Article 5) If any member of the joint guarantee is promoted, demoted, resigns, withdraws, or dies, the guarantors shall find another joint guarantee within ten days. (Article 6) If any member of the joint guarantee is found to be transporting or providing lamps for smoking opium and drugs and it is confirmed to be true, in addition to dismissing all co-guarantors and confiscating their security deposit, the perpetrator of the transportation or provision of lamps for smoking opium and drugs shall be handed over to the legal authorities for handling according to law. (Article 7) After the implementation of these regulations, each ship shall complete the procedures within two months and submit the list of joint guarantees to the shipping bureau for submission to the competent authorities for filing. Subsequent joint guarantees shall be reported at any time. Any ship that fails to provide guarantees in accordance with the rules within the time limit shall be ordered by the shipping bureau to suspend their duties. (Article 8) These regulations shall be implemented after being submitted by the provincial government to the Chairman of the Military Commission and Superintendent General of Opium Suppression for approval."

Jianguo Ship Escapes Danger and Sails On After Being Agrounded on the Liu River Beach for Approximately Ten Hours 97

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River ship Jianguo ran aground at the mouth of the Liu River at 8:30 a.m. on the 4th. Details were published in yesterday's newspaper. The company has now received a report from the Jianguo ship stating that the cause of the grounding was heavy fog outside the mouth of Wusong and an inaccurate compass on the ship. It is now learned that the ship was able to back out of the shallows and leave the beach on its own during high tide that afternoon, thanks to the efforts of Captain Huang Youzhi. The tugboat arrived, but it was not needed. The grounding lasted about ten hours, and the ship has now resumed its voyage to Hankou as usual.

Fanwangdu: As winter approaches and the weather turns cold, the north wind has been raging for days, making it feel even colder. Even with cotton clothing, it still feels thin at night. They were unable to resist and were all robbed and imprisoned, with one robber guarding them with a gun. The remaining robbers began searching the house and left after about ten minutes, fleeing north. After checking the losses, it was found that more than 180 yuan in cash, silk, woolen clothes, and other items had been stolen. The case was reported to the Guangfulu Substation of the Caojiadu Branch Bureau and a request was made for pursuit and arrest.

Zhoujiazui Road: A family surnamed Mou at 56, Lane 416, Zhoujiazui Road was robbed by several robbers at approximately 6:00 p.m. yesterday evening. Strict Prohibition of "Catching Fallen Cotton" in Wusong 101

Groups of Vagrants Stealing Affect Rural Areas Significantly

Due to the continuous rainstorms in the spring and summer of this year, the growth of cotton and rice planted in the farmland of the four townships of Wusong was delayed, resulting in a poor autumn harvest. Even now, the cotton bolls have not fully opened. Unemployed vagrants believe that the time has come and are forming groups to steal fallen cotton everywhere, which has a significant impact on rural areas. In light of this, the Wusong District Farmers' Association has requested the police to issue a notice to strictly prohibit the practice. The notice reads as follows: "In response to a letter from the Shanghai Wusong District Farmers' Association, based on a report from farmers stating that 'It is often the case at the beginning of winter in each district that a general public of unemployed people goes to the various villages to pick cotton (commonly known as catching fallen cotton). This autumn, the cotton harvests in each village have been poor, and most of the bolls have not yet opened. If this is not prohibited, it will have a significant impact on the future of the rural areas. Therefore, we request that you investigate and approve the issuance of a strict prohibition to maintain agriculture, etc.' If you continue to pick cotton or are reported, you will be severely punished once the investigation is complete. This notice is hereby issued for general knowledge. Deng Zhiyi, Director."

The total amount of customs gold exchange note reserve is 586,679.80 yuan. In accordance with Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the gold reserve should be at least 60%, with the remainder being guaranteed by legal collateral. To the esteemed editor:

Having read in the local news column of your newspaper on October 31st a report on the Hu Nanshan Tang pharmacy's accidental dispensing of the wrong prescription, although the content is purely a record of court testimony, the headline "Hu Nanshan Tang Pharmacy Accidentally Dispenses Wrong Prescription" seems inaccurate. Moreover, Hu Nanshan's accusation against Ding Jinrong et al. for extortion also has its own reasonable basis. In the future, when the truth comes to light, it may elicit sighs from people in society about the difficulty of opening a pharmacy. At this time, when the turbulent waves of recession are raging, people's hearts are difficult to fathom with normal sentiment. We have always admired your newspaper's upholding of fairness and justice. Therefore, we specially submit this request, hoping for your clear discernment and that you will kindly publish this letter in the correspondence column. We would be endlessly grateful. Sincerely, the Shanghai National Medicine Industry Association, November 5th, to the esteemed chief editor of local news at Shen Bao.

An Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce Edited by the China Credit Information Service 112

Publication Launch

Shanghai is the hub of the nation's industry and commerce, so the prosperity or decline of Shanghai's industry and commerce has a significant impact on the entire country. The Service has been collecting a considerable amount of information on various industrial and commercial sectors as part of its mission. Going forward, we plan to publish articles in this publication on a weekly basis, each focusing on a specific industry or commercial sector, with the aim of systematically providing readers with the latest information on the realities of industry and commerce, the causes of successes and failures, and future trends, in order to contribute our humble knowledge. However, given the magnitude of the subject, omissions and errors are inevitable. We hope that all sectors will correct and teach us. We would be immensely grateful.

A Brief Overview of Changes in Shanghai's Industry and Commerce Over the Past Three Years

I. Introduction

According to credit information services and other statistical agencies in various countries, there are statistics on "Business Failure" and "New Capital Issue." To assess the general trends in the rise and fall of industry and commerce, one can use price indices and market experience for estimation. However, to further study the reasons for the successes and failures of various industries, future trends, and the mutual influence between various industries, one must focus on the aforementioned two statistics. Since its establishment, the Service has also paid considerable attention to collecting this information. However, among businesses in various countries, most of those with some scale are corporate organizations, and the issuance of stocks and bonds is documented in official records. The situation in China's industrial and commercial sector is different. Corporate organizations are few in number, and most stores are unregistered. It is nearly impossible to gather statistics on new capital issues. The "business failure" category is easily confused by terms such as "reorganization" and "capital increase." Strictly speaking, "reorganization" and "capital increase" can be said to encompass the dissolution of old businesses and the establishment of new businesses. In reality, the situation is not as severe as it appears. After careful consideration, our colleagues have listed the standards for data collection as three categories: new establishments, reorganizations, and closures. While the "reorganization" category is not as severe as "closures," reorganizations inevitably increase during market downturns, and their trend is generally similar to closures, with minor differences. This article will analyze and study the number of new establishments, reorganizations, and closures of Shanghai's industrial and commercial businesses from 1933 to June of this year. The data collection methods mainly rely on various daily newspapers, supplemented by the Service's regular investigations. Small-scale new establishments and closures that are not reported in newspapers and that have no dealings with the financial industry are likely to be overlooked. In addition, data collection methods have been significantly improved over the years, which may also affect the numbers. We hope readers will pay attention to this.

II. Changes in Figures Over the Past Three Years

Since the outbreak of the global economic panic in 1929, China has presented an appearance of prosperity due to the protection of low silver prices. However, as the global economic panic deepened, with the "September 18th Incident" in Shenyang and the "January 28th Incident" in Shanghai externally, and the abandonment of the gold standard by various countries, resulting in a rebound in silver prices, and internal natural disasters of floods and droughts and frequent disturbances, the national economy was severely affected. The manifestations of this were particularly evident in Shanghai. The changes in figures over the past three years are listed in the table below for comparison:

New Establishments Reorganizations Closures

1933 100 100 100

1934 80.40 2,116.14 171.05

1935 54.87 3,054.53 233.71

Using the average monthly figures for 1933 as a base, the rise and fall of the change index over the past three years is as follows...

As shown in the table on the right, the new establishment index has declined annually in the past three years. Compared to 1933, the new establishment index has decreased by 45.13%, the closure index has increased by more than two times, and the reorganization index has increased dramatically to more than thirty times.

The detailed monthly change figures for the entire year of 1934 and the first six months of this year are listed below (unit: one business):

The most reorganizations in 1934 were in March, April, and October, and in the first half of 1935, they were in March and April. The most closures in 1934 were in May and August, and in the first half of 1935, they were in January and June. In the past, changes often occurred during seasonal closures, but now this seasonality seems to have been lost. (To be continued)
